<div id="review_2043446214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043446214" />
    <a title="Gabby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby"><img alt="Gabby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482222518p2/26560207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043446214?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabby" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby">Gabby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=favorite-female-characters">favorite-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=liked-it">liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=4-star-books">4-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043446214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13205441405443532981"><b>This book was so cute.</b> I've read a few Kasie West novels now, and I think this one is my favorite. This is a light and fluffy YA contemporary novel that follows this girl named Abby who is a painter, and she desperately wants her paintings displayed in this art show, but she is sad when she shows her boss her paintings and he rejects her and says her paintings need "more heart". So Abby creates a list of experiences she feels like she needs to have in order to become a better painter. She's also</span>
  <span id="freeText13205441405443532981" style="display:none"><b>This book was so cute.</b> I've read a few Kasie West novels now, and I think this one is my favorite. This is a light and fluffy YA contemporary novel that follows this girl named Abby who is a painter, and she desperately wants her paintings displayed in this art show, but she is sad when she shows her boss her paintings and he rejects her and says her paintings need "more heart". So Abby creates a list of experiences she feels like she needs to have in order to become a better painter. She's also secretly but no so secretly in love with her best friend Cooper, and their friendship/romance was the cutest.<br /><br /><b>I love Abby as a main character</b> and I feel like I relate to her a lot. She admits that she fears change and she prefers to live life in her safe bubble, which is something I totally understand. I loved her family dynamics - her Mother who never leaves the house, her Dad who is away from home serving in the military and writes hilarious emails, and her Grandpa who is probably the funniest, most sarcastic character in the whole book. I love her friendship with Cooper, their chemistry jumped right off the page and I was smiling every time I read their scenes together. The only reason I knocked off a star is because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the whole love triangle with Cooper and Iris and Abby got a little too ridiculous for me. Iris telling Abby she needs to back off and them both fighting for him just started feeling a little too YA if that makes sense... Idk Iris's character in general just bothered me. She felt like such a typical cliche mean girl with nothing more to her character. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The ending actually made me tear up a little, which I was super shocked by. I wasn't expecting to get so emotionally attached to these characters, but I did!<br /><br />Overall, this was a really cute, light fun read and it was exactly what I needed right now! I can't decide if this book or P.S. I Like You is my favorite Kasie West book I've read so far! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13205441405443532981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=1-and-a-half-stars">1-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=angsts-and-angsts">angsts-and-angsts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=nooo-stop-the-pining">nooo-stop-the-pining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=eh">eh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=annoying-tropes">annoying-tropes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=give-me-back-my-heart">give-me-back-my-heart</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087045511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13534946089703246546">I simultaneously love and hate reading this book. There are so many things that irked me, mainly how Abby pined over her best friend whom she confessed to a year ago and he pretended to think it was a joke. I was def not shipping him with her, although he seemed an all right friend at times. However, despite my huge irritation and dislike that she loved him while he was dating another girl – I felt like it was all part of the journey. She was on a rollercoaster of emotions, and I was on it with </span>
  <span id="freeText13534946089703246546" style="display:none">I simultaneously love and hate reading this book. There are so many things that irked me, mainly how Abby pined over her best friend whom she confessed to a year ago and he pretended to think it was a joke. I was def not shipping him with her, although he seemed an all right friend at times. However, despite my huge irritation and dislike that she loved him while he was dating another girl – I felt like it was all part of the journey. She was on a rollercoaster of emotions, and I was on it with her. I cried. Despite me not liking this potential pairing, I still hurt with her and died a little bit inside with her when she saw him with someone else.<br /><br />And truly, I was confused with her because the question was, “Did he love her back because he was too afraid of losing her? Or did he recently started loving her? Or did he just see her as platonic?” I kept on going back between all of them <br /><br /><b>Now, ignore everything that I just said. Fuck, I need to stop starting a review, when I still have a quarter left of the book. Now that I’m done, my opinion has changed. I’m just gonna go straight ahead to spoilers. BE WARNED.</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OK, so I was hoping this book is about Abby finally realizing that Cooper isn’t worth it after he reveals he doesn’t love her, and learns to be ready for changes, even if that means losing someone you once thought you loved. And then, they’ll be great friends again, but not best friends like they used to be. <br /><br />But he loves her. Like, what??? I mean tbh there were a lot of signs, and I had a feeling he did (there were a lot of signs that he did). But then, I got thrown off towards the end when he fucked up and she decided to want space from him.<br /><br />Idk idk. I just super hate romances where the girl pines after a guy especially while he is in a relationship with another girl. It would be one thing if it was just one-sided love, and the protagonist learns to accept the rejection and move on. But wait, he lvoes her, so did I really spend a whole book reading him dating someone else, while the girl pined and gave him 1000000% effort. Meanwhile, he missed her art show, and let her down by not picking up her mom to take her to the art show ON THE DAY she was gonna confess her love to him (again). And he did not just missed it, he was on a fuckin’ date with the girl he has been dating this whole book.<br /><br />But then, he realized he has loved Abby all along. <br /><br />OK, sure. Whatever. I’m not here for it. Cooper is an all right character. He’s funny and a cool friend, but dang I hate him as a love interest. I felt like the message would have been stronger to see her move on from a guy who didn’t appreciate her before. Especially since he ignored her first confession of love a year ago and laughed it off because he was too afraid to love her. And then, he dates a lot of girls while she pines after him.<br />No, no, no, no. Good friend, but it was painful to read as a love interest. I liked Elliot a lot more and he didn’t even have many scenes. I guess I like the IDEA of him, the potential that could’ve been. I rather have a fresh start with the potential in him, than the angstiness of what Abby already had with Cooper.<br /><br /><br />That’s just my opinion anyway. My pet peeve is reading a book about a girl who pines after a guy. But I can learn to appreciate the book because I can sympathize, and cheer for her when she finally realizes she deserves better and moves on. Actually, I LOVE books that despite irritating me, can make me feel so much and root for the character’s slow and steady growth out of heartbreak and onto something better.<br /><br />But since that did not happened here, that appreciation was lost. <br /><br />I’m sure a lot of people would like Cooper. And I do – he has funny dialogue and he’s sweet. I just can’t stand the idea of a romance where a girl pines over a guy who doesn’t love her back (even if he does end up realizing he loves her later on) and who was dating other girls while she pined. And she actually tried to “steal him” back from Iris by confessing her love to him while he’s still dating Iris. I mean it’s one thing to just admit your feelings to him and see what he says, but for her to plot a plan for a big love confession and kiss is a bit unclassy IMO. Also, I didn’t like the female jealousy and pettiness between Abby and Iris. Iris is portrayed a bitch, so no doubt I didn’t want her with Cooper either. But ugh, why did we have to go down this path? Anyway, all of this was not my cup of tea, so naturally, I can’t like this book because it went to a direction that I wasn’t feeing.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So besides what I just said above, I do love that Abby learns to make changes in her life that makes her braver through experiences. I love her new friendship with Lacey, and I really felt for the scenes where Lacey comforted her during hard times.<br /><br />Also, I appreciate the family aspect. Her grandfather is hilarious. His and Abby’s sarcasm are so on point, and I can relate on so many levels. And her emails to her dad is sweet. I would have liked to see a scene where he finally comes back. Her mom is good too. I am proud of her growth as well. <br /><br />Sooooo… With that being all said, I have to give this ugh I don’t know. Because 97% of my opinion comes from the ending, I am gonna have to give this <b>1.5 stars</b>. It just does not click with me personally, even though I get why things turned out that way. I just wanted something else. If it went in the other direction that what my earlier review went in, I probably would have given this 3 stars. But it didn’t so oh well. <br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. Not my cup of tea with the direction this book went in for overall plot, but the ending was indeed happy. If you liked what happened in my above spoiler, then you probably love the ending. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? Other things to note? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So it’s like a square going on. Elliot is interested in Abby. Abby loves Cooper. Cooper and Iris are dating. <br /><br />High angst. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I cried because there was this one scene that broke my heart as I sympathized with progatonist. But not a generally depressing book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Humorous bantering, but not necessarily a book of humor. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scenes? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Lacey invited Abby to her house as they ate ice cream and watched movies to get over a heartbreak. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Targeted for teens. Nothing inappropriate here though so any age can work. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />-----------<br />I’m a sucker for any Kasie West books #sorrynotsorry</span>
  <a data-text-id="13534946089703246546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063540436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5709760496117938598">Absolutely LOVED! Full review to come closer to release date.<br/><br/>*EDITED TO ADD REVIEW*<br/>I have always loved Kasie West's stories. From her endearing characters to the heartfelt story line that always leaves you with a smile on your face by the end. But there are some, that just resonate with me and Love, Life and The List was one such story.<br/><br/>I connected so much with Abby in a deeper emotional level than I thought I would. In some areas she spoke to me in ways that I haven't had happen in a YA story in</span>
  <span id="freeText5709760496117938598" style="display:none">Absolutely LOVED! Full review to come closer to release date.<br /><br />*EDITED TO ADD REVIEW*<br />I have always loved Kasie West's stories. From her endearing characters to the heartfelt story line that always leaves you with a smile on your face by the end. But there are some, that just resonate with me and Love, Life and The List was one such story.<br /><br />I connected so much with Abby in a deeper emotional level than I thought I would. In some areas she spoke to me in ways that I haven't had happen in a YA story in a really long time and because of it, I simply couldn't put this down. I read it in one sitting and barely even took breaks to get a drink or answer a text. Something about Abby's story just spoke to me and I can't even say for sure why other than West is just an amazing writer and just knows how to put enough emotion and depth into her stories and characters that almost anyone can't help but love them and feel for them. <br /><br />This truly was a favorite from West and a story that I won't be forgetting anytime soon. I love when an author can speak to you and change you and worm their way into your very soul and West succeeded brilliantly here in doing so. <br /><br /><br />*ARC provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.*</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2Lxje7fjyK4FChGvPELWKBJQkulQqt8wQH2DTmSy0SidWk2aYyXAZiMRRAiDO4wnPEcUS1SRTz1QpCbAmJXObA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MgZbP9mPBdFMR85/tO9W65s/3F4sG0b8ft94Fd5bmHR34HXeDUkNGWpcm9gLlgzktSha/Cgg1vFuBt2bInyHMA==')})
  }

        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>

    </div>
